\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: If $x$ is a positive integer and $x(x + 1)(x + 2)(x + 3) + 1 = 379^2,$ compute $x.$
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: Find the ordered pair $(a,b)$ of real numbers for which $x^2+ax+b$ has a non-real root whose cube is $343$.
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

The answer is -2x-1

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: Find constants $A,$ $B,$ $C,$ and $D$ so that
\[\frac{x^3 + 3x^2 - 12x + 36}{x^4 - 16} = \frac{A}{x - 2} + \frac{B}{x + 2} + \frac{Cx + D}{x^2 + 4}.\]Enter the ordered quadruple $(A,B,C,D).$
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: The set of real numbers $x$ for which
$$\dfrac{1}{x-2009}+\dfrac{1}{x-2010}+\dfrac{1}{x-2011}\ge 1$$is the union of intervals of the form $a<x\le b$. What is the sum of the lengths of these intervals?
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Jonathon is given the following problem: Let $a$ and $b$ be positive real numbers such that $a + b = 1.$  Find the minimum value of
\[\left( a + \frac{1}{a} \right)^2 + \left( b + \frac{1}{b} \right)^2.\]Jonathon reasons as follows: By AM-GM,
\[a + \frac{1}{a} \ge 2,\]and
\[b + \frac{1}{b} \ge 2,\]so
\[\left( a + \frac{1}{a} \right)^2 + \left( b + \frac{1}{b} \right)^2 \ge 2^2 + 2^2 = 8.\]He concludes that the minimum value is 8, but this answer is incorrect.  What is the minimum value?

As a bonus, determine where Jonathon went wrong.
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}

&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$

|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: Compute
\[\sum_{n = 1}^\infty \frac{1}{F_n F_{n + 2}},\]where $F_n$ denotes the $n$th Fibonacci number, so $F_0 = 0$ and $F_1 = 1.$
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: At a competition with $N$ players, the number of players given elite status is equal to $2^{1+\lfloor \log_{2} (N-1) \rfloor}-N$. Suppose that $19$ players are given elite status. What is the sum of the two smallest possible values of $N$?
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: The graph of $y = f(x)$ is shown below.

[asy]
unitsize(0.5 cm);

real func(real x) {
  return (log(x));
}

int i, n;

for (i = -5; i <= 5; ++i) {
  draw((i,-5)--(i,5),gray(0.7));
  draw((-5,i)--(5,i),gray(0.7));
}

draw((-5,0)--(5,0),Arrows(6));
draw((0,-5)--(0,5),Arrows(6));

label("$x$", (5,0), E);
label("$y$", (0,5), N);

draw(graph(func,exp(-5),5),red);

label("$y = f(x)$", (3,-2), UnFill);
[/asy]

Which is the graph of $y = f^{-1}(x)$?

[asy]
unitsize(0.5 cm);

picture[] graf;
int i, n;

real func(real x) {
  return (log(x));
}

path foo = graph(func,exp(-5),5); 

for (n = 1; n <= 5; ++n) {
  graf[n] = new picture;
  for (i = -5; i <= 5; ++i) {
    draw(graf[n],(i,-5)--(i,5),gray(0.7));
    draw(graf[n],(-5,i)--(5,i),gray(0.7));
  }
  draw(graf[n],(-5,0)--(5,0),Arrows(6));
  draw(graf[n],(0,-5)--(0,5),Arrows(6));

  label(graf[n],"$x$", (5,0), E);
  label(graf[n],"$y$", (0,5), N);
}

draw(graf[1],reflect((0,0),(0,1))*foo,red);
draw(graf[2],reflect((0,0),(1,-1))*foo,red);
draw(graf[3],reflect((0,0),(1,0))*foo,red);
draw(graf[4],rotate(180)*foo,red);
draw(graf[5],reflect((0,0),(1,1))*foo,red);

label(graf[1], "A", (0,-6));
label(graf[2], "B", (0,-6));
label(graf[3], "C", (0,-6));
label(graf[4], "D", (0,-6));
label(graf[5], "E", (0,-6));

add(graf[1]);
add(shift((12,0))*(graf[2]));
add(shift((24,0))*(graf[3]));
add(shift((6,-12))*(graf[4]));
add(shift((18,-12))*(graf[5]));
[/asy]

Enter the letter of the graph of $y = f^{-1}(x).$
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: What is the value of the following expression: $1 - 3 + 5 - 7 + 9 - \cdots - 43 + 45 - 47 + 49$ ?
Q: Let $z$ be a complex number with $|z| = \sqrt{2}.$  Find the maximum value of
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)|.\]
A: Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Since $|z| = \sqrt{2},$ $x^2 + y^2 = 2.$  Then
\begin{align*}
|z - 1| &= |x + yi - 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x - 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 - 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{3 - 2x},
\end{align*}and
\begin{align*}
|z + 1| &= |x + yi + 1| \\
&= \sqrt{(x + 1)^2 + y^2} \\
&= \sqrt{x^2 + 2x + 1 + 2 - x^2} \\
&= \sqrt{2x + 3},
\end{align*}so
\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: The foci of the ellipse $\frac{x^2}{49} + \frac{y^2}{33} = 1$ are $F_1$ and $F_2,$ as shown below.  Let $P$ be a point on the circle $x^2 + (y - 3)^2 = 4.$  Line $F_2 P$ intersects the ellipse again at $Q,$ where the $y$-coordinate of $Q$ is positive.  Find the maximum value of $PQ + F_1 Q.$

[asy]
unitsize(0.4 cm);

pair P, Q;
pair[] F;

path ell = yscale(sqrt(33))*xscale(7)*Circle((0,0),1);
F[1] = (4,0);
F[2] = (-4,0);
P = (0,3) + 2*dir(240);
Q = intersectionpoint(P--interp(F[2],P,5),ell);

draw(ell);
draw((-8,0)--(8,0));
draw((0,-7)--(0,7));
draw(Circle((0,3),2));
draw(F[1]--Q--F[2]);

dot("$F_1$", F[1], S);
dot("$F_2$", F[2], S);
dot("$P$", P, S);
label("$Q$", Q, NE);
[/asy]

\[|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}.\]Thus, we want to maximize $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3),$ subject to $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2}.$

We claim the maximum occurs at $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$  At $x = -\frac{1}{2},$ $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = 32.$  Note that
\[32 - (3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) = -8x^3 + 12x^2 + 18x + 5 = (2x + 1)^2 (5 - 2x) \ge 0,\]so $(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3) \le 32$ for $-\sqrt{2} \le x \le \sqrt{2},$ with equality if and only if $x = -\frac{1}{2}.$

Therefore, the maximum value of $|(z - 1)^2 (z + 1)| = \sqrt{(3 - 2x)^2 (2x + 3)}$ is $\sqrt{32} = \boxed{4 \sqrt{2}}.$
The answer is 4 \sqrt{2}

Q: Suppose $f(x) = x^2,$ and $g(x)$ is a polynomial such that $f(g(x)) = 4x^2 + 4x + 1$. Enter all possible polynomials $g(x),$ separated by commas.
A: Since $f(x)=x^2$, $f(g(x))=g(x)^2$. Therefore, $g(x)^2=4x^2+4x+1=(2x+1)^2$ and $g(x)=\boxed{2x+1}$ or $g(x)=\boxed{-2x-1}$.
The answer is -2x-1

Q: If the parabola defined by $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x,$ then calculate the constant $a.$
A: The parabola $y = ax^2 + 6$ is tangent to the line $y = x$ when the equation
\[ax^2 + 6 = x\]has a double root (which is the $x$-coordinate of the point of tangency).  From this equation,
\[ax^2 - x + 6 = 0.\]This quadratic has a double root when the discriminant is 0, which gives us $1 - 24a = 0.$  Hence, $a = \boxed{\frac{1}{24}}.$
The answer is \frac{1}{24}

Q: Compute
\[\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb.\]
A: The $n$th term of the series is given by
\[\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2}.\]Note that
\begin{align*}
(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2 &= [(4n + 3) + (4n - 1)][(4n + 3) - (4n - 1)] \\
&= (8n + 2)(4) = 8(4n + 1),
\end{align*}so we can write
\begin{align*}
\frac{4n + 1}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} &= \frac{1}{8} \left[ \frac{(4n + 3)^2 - (4n - 1)^2}{(4n - 1)^2 (4n + 3)^2} \right] \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{(4n - 1)^2} - \frac{1}{(4n + 3)^2} \right).
\end{align*}Thus,
\begin{align*}
\frac{5}{3^2 \cdot 7^2} + \frac{9}{7^2 \cdot 11^2} + \frac{13}{11^2 \cdot 15^2} + \dotsb &= \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{3^2} - \frac{1}{7^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{7^2} - \frac{1}{11^2} \right) + \frac{1}{8} \left( \frac{1}{11^2} - \frac{1}{15^2} \right) + \dotsb \\
&= \frac{1}{8} \cdot \frac{1}{3^2} = \boxed{\frac{1}{72}}.
\end{align*}
The answer is \frac{1}{72}

Q: Consider all polynomials of a complex variable, $P(z)=4z^4+az^3+bz^2+cz+d$, where $a,b,c,$ and $d$ are integers, $0\le d\le c\le b\le a\le 4$, and the polynomial has a zero $z_0$ with $|z_0|=1.$ What is the sum of all values $P(1)$ over all the polynomials with these properties?
